  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_531bd3d6-bceb-417d-a22c-9b7a2277d38f'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer15546350963482008723">THE SECRET OF THE DRAGONS<br/><br/>Vetch was an Altan serf working the land which had once been his family's farm. Young and slight, Vetch would have died of overwork, exposure, and starvation if not for the anger which was his only real sustenance--anger that he had lost his home and family in a war of conquest waged by the dragon-riding Jousters of Tia. Tia had usurped nearly halt</span>
  <span id="freeText15546350963482008723" style="display:none">THE SECRET OF THE DRAGONS<br /><br />Vetch was an Altan serf working the land which had once been his family's farm. Young and slight, Vetch would have died of overwork, exposure, and starvation if not for the anger which was his only real sustenance--anger that he had lost his home and family in a war of conquest waged by the dragon-riding Jousters of Tia. Tia had usurped nearly halt of Alta's lands and enslaved or killed many of Vetch's countrymen. Sometimes it seemed that his entire cruel fate revolved around dragons and the Jousters who rode them.<br /><br />But his fate changed forever the day he first saw a dragon.<br /><br />From its narrow, golden, large-eyed head, to its pointed emerald ears, to the magnificent blue wings, the dragon was a thing of multicolored, jeweled beauty, slim and supple and quite as large as the shed it perched on. Vetch, almost failed to notice the Jouster who stood beside him. "I need a boy," the rider had said, and suddenly Vetch found himself lifted above the earth and transported by dragon-back to a different world.<br /><br />Vetch was to be trained as a dragon-boy, and he hardly believed his luck. The compound seemed like paradise: he could eat until he was full, and all he had to do was care for his Jouster's dragon, Kashet.<br /><br />It didn't take long for Vetch to realize that Kashet was special--for unlike other dragons, Kashet was gentle by nature and did not need the tranquilizing tala plant to make her tracttable. Vetch became determined to learn the secret of how Kashet had been tamed. For if Kashet could be tamed, perhaps Vetch could tame a dragon of his own. And if he could, then he might be able to escape and bring the secret of dragon-taming back to his homeland of Alta. And that secret, might prove to be the key to Alta's liberation....</span>
  <a data-text-id="15546350963482008723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2601754485" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2601754485" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2601754485?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2601754485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16000624129529391736"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>Books like these make me nostalgic for childhood, when I would stay up way past my bedtime reading books with a flashlight, so utterly absorbed that it felt like I was physically unable to put the book down. Mercedes Lackey is an amazing fantasy author who is not afraid to write about serious subjects, strong women, and LGBT characters, and even though she's been around forever, not nearly enough people know about her or read her books. </span>
  <span id="freeText16000624129529391736" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>Books like these make me nostalgic for childhood, when I would stay up way past my bedtime reading books with a flashlight, so utterly absorbed that it felt like I was physically unable to put the book down. Mercedes Lackey is an amazing fantasy author who is not afraid to write about serious subjects, strong women, and LGBT characters, and even though she's been around forever, not nearly enough people know about her or read her books. My job today is to try and fix that by telling you about the awesomeness that is JOUST.<br><br><br><br>Vetch is a serf tied to his land. He is an Altan, a country that is at war with the Tians. His Tian master is cruel and abuses him all day as he toils under the hot sun farming finicky root vegetables, and his only solace comes from cursing his master and wishing him ill. One day, one of the dragon riders called Jousters comes to the land to borrow some water and witnesses the extreme abuse Vetch suffers at the hands of his master. Shocked by such a brazen display of cruelty, the Jouster, named Ari, steals Vetch away to become a dragon boy. At this compound, his new job is to tend to the soldiers' dragons and try to anticipate both their and their riders' every need.<br><br><br><br>Ari, his savior, is different from other Jousters. He is the only rider to have hand-raised his dragon from the egg, and the difference in behavior shows. However, the work and time involved have kept others from doing this. Vetch, however, who is no stranger to hard work, can't get the idea out of his head. Even though he loves his new job working with the dragons, the cognitive dissonance of working for the selfsame army that oppresses his people does not escape him. And when one of the dragons at the compound goes into heat, suddenly the possibility of getting his own egg to hatch and raise seems more than just a pipe dream. The risk could be deadly. But the payoff could affect <i>wars</i>.<br><br><br><br>From the beginning, I found myself immersed in this world. Vetch is a great protagonist, selfish and impulsive at times, but also endearingly idealistic and naive. His outsider status makes him relatable to anyone who has ever felt like they didn't belong, and watching him get revenge through patience and hard work is incredibly satisfying. I also loved the descriptions of the dragons, and how each had their own personalities. Dragons are some of my favorite fantasy creatures, and I loved, loved, <i>loved </i>how Vetch's every day tasks with the dragons were so well thought out and detailed. It really added to this world, which was clearly inspired by ancient Egypt, and made it feel vivid and realistic.<br><br><br><br>If you're into classic high fantasy that is intelligent, deep, and not too dark, Mercedes Lackey is an excellent pick. She has her ups and downs with her books, but man, when she nails it, she freaking nails it. JOUST is a must-read if you love dragons and magic. I can't stress that enough.<br><br><br><br>4 to 4.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="16000624129529391736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_9411661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9411661" />
    <a title="Joana Rodriguez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/634615-joana-rodriguez"><img alt="Joana Rodriguez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195697348p2/634615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9411661?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joana Rodriguez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joana Rodriguez" href="/user/show/634615-joana-rodriguez">Joana Rodriguez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy and dragon lovers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9411661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15970148678219292789">As a dragon enthusiast I jumped for joy when I found this book on the bookshelf at my local bookstore. After I read it I couldn’t help but think that this was what a dragon book should be. Mercedes Lackey has always been one of my favorite fantasy writers and in this book she proves why she deserves all of the praise that she gets. Fans of Anne McGaffry’s Dragonriders of Pern series will not be disappointed in this book. Despite the fact that Joust revolves around dragonriders, referred to as Jo</span>
  <span id="freeText15970148678219292789" style="display:none">As a dragon enthusiast I jumped for joy when I found this book on the bookshelf at my local bookstore. After I read it I couldn’t help but think that this was what a dragon book should be. Mercedes Lackey has always been one of my favorite fantasy writers and in this book she proves why she deserves all of the praise that she gets. Fans of Anne McGaffry’s Dragonriders of Pern series will not be disappointed in this book. Despite the fact that Joust revolves around dragonriders, referred to as Jousters, Lackey’s book is a new and refreshing read that stands alone and alongside the Dragonriders of Pern series.<br /><br />The story follows the adventures of Vetch an Altan surf, just another of the spoils of the Altan - Tian conflict. Vetch was merely a farmer’s son until the day the Tian army declared possesion of their farm after having gained more ground in the war. Before his eyes he saw his father murdered, his sister beaten, their possessions stolen, and then he and his family were placed into a life worse than slavery. Torn from his family Vetch is forced to serve a cruel master. Khefti the Fat, his master, continuously beats, starves, and overworks Vetch while his apprentices take great pleasure in tormenting him. This continues on for several years until the day Jouster Ari arrives at Khefti’s to stop for a drink of water and a small respite from patrols. There Ari witnesses first hand the harsh labor that Vetch undergoes and the treatment he receives. Seizing upon the law that states all Jousters may requisition anything they need within reason, Ari states he is need of a boy to tend his dragon and carries Vetch off to the compound.<br /><br />Vetch’s lot improves greatly here where food is in abundance and he is treated with a measure of respect. In fact Vetch at times has trouble remembering the hate and anger that kept him going while working for Khefti. I found this to be exceptionally well done and played out. Throughout Joust Vetch is undergoing a major development. He began the story as an angry, spiteful, and vengeful child who was no longer really a child. Vetch’s existence was a miserable one and the only thing that kept him going was his stubborn will to live on despite the hardships, but the thing that fueled him the most was his anger and hatred for the Tians.<br /><br />While Vetch is at the compound he begins to realize that the atrocities inflicted upon his people by Tian soldiers do not reflect the attitudes of all Tians alike. Indeed at one point he is even shocked to realize that he does not pray for Ari’s defeat, as he initially had, but that Ari would always return safe because Ari had become his friend.<br /><br />As time passes on Vetch becomes as dragon obsessed as his Jouster but with the bravery and hope that only the young [and foolhardy] can have Vetch endeavors to purloin a dragon egg of his own to hatch and raise. The Great Tian King has ordered that the number of Jousters in the skies be doubled so that the Altans can be at long last crushed and Vetch seeks to learn how to the methods of raising a tame dragon to the Altans to shift the tides of the war.<br /><br />Lackey’s story is beautifully told, the amount of detail an attention paid to the dragons is astounding. The reader’s mind will be filled with visions of dragons and soaring above the clouds long after they have finished the book. To top it off the setting for Lackey’s world is a sort of alternate ancient Egypt which gives the setting an extra touch of exoticness that somehow makes the world seem familiar and different all at the same time. Young and old readers, be they fantasy buffs, or just bookworms will adore this first book in an exciting series.<br /><br />You can <a href="http://review.nanashi-inc.net/?p=19" rel="nofollow noopener">read the original book review here</a> and my reviews for other books as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15970148678219292789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10901992312112236869" style="display:none">I'm going to call this a 3.5. This is a fun, easy to read book about a boy and dragons. Yes, there are some books out there with similar ideas, but pretty much every fantasy book out there is borrowing ideas or influenced by other authors.<br /><br />I found parts of the book to be a bit slow, but I liked Vetch and the dragons. I did think that Vetch said things that were way too grown-up sounding for a 10-12 year old kid though. For example, he said something to Ari like "If you don't talk about this you're just going to snap". <br /><br />Overall I liked it, I would recommend it if you like books that have dragons in them.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17620484201651701586">It's been so long since I first read this that I only had the vaguest ideas of what would happen and how, so this was a really fun re-read with my book club on Discord. I love Lackey's approach to dragons and their relationships with humans here, and the strong nods to Egyptian culture throughout are well done and enjoyed. I'm not sure when I'll have time to keep reading the series, but I know I need to since I never read the fourth book during my initial reading.</span>

<div id="review_68250495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68250495" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/396706-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68250495?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/396706-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/396706-ann?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68250495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10436995386608289093">I was something of a Mercedes Lackey fan when her earliest books came out -- not a fanatical fan by any means, but I read and sought out the subsequent Valdemar books as they came out. Somewhere along the way I moved on to other things, and the reviews on her later offerings didn't motivate me to return.<br/><br/>I picked up Joust recently, in part because I was looking for a book of a certain length to read at a 10-12 pages a night from mid-August through September. This turned out to be an ideal book fo</span>
  <span id="freeText10436995386608289093" style="display:none">I was something of a Mercedes Lackey fan when her earliest books came out -- not a fanatical fan by any means, but I read and sought out the subsequent Valdemar books as they came out. Somewhere along the way I moved on to other things, and the reviews on her later offerings didn't motivate me to return.<br /><br />I picked up Joust recently, in part because I was looking for a book of a certain length to read at a 10-12 pages a night from mid-August through September. This turned out to be an ideal book for my purposes -- it was a pleasant enough read to keep me on track, but not riveting enough to tempt me to read more than my 10 pages.<br /><br />There's actually a really good coming-of-age fantasy book somewhere in here just waiting for an aggressive editor to break it out. Lackey has done a great job creating a fantasy world set in a world much like ancient Egypt (if a little too westernized for a truly different fantasy novel). <br /><br />Vetch is a serf boy rescued from oppressive servitude by one of the Great King's Jousters (dragon-riders who patrol the kingdom's borders). The novel follows Vetch as he settles into his new position as dragon-boy, learns the ropes, excels, and fixes on the idea of hatching a dragon of his own.<br /><br />Not much really happens beyond that in this 384 page novel. We're treated to long passages on Vetch's duties as a dragon boy, the care and training of dragons, the duties of the Jousters, Vetch's day to day resentments, attachments, worries, and lessons learned. That all this carries the story through 384 pages is a testament to how well Lackey has developed this world and the people and dragons who inhabit it. <br /><br />Unfortunately, with only three characters who have major speaking roles, the story itself wears thin. The plot's bogginess isn't helped by the author's tendency to repeat herself numerous times, or when she allows Vetch to veer off into multi-page worries that turn out to have no bearing on how the story actually turns out. A paring down of the book by about 1/5 might have helped get things moving along without sacrificing anything important.<br /><br />Still, an engaging story, and the jousting dragons are interesting creatures with a believable biology. I may pick up the sequel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10436995386608289093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21146505" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21146505" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1122115-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303844711p2/1122115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21146505?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/1122115-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People new to stories involving dragons</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Allison by: </span>
      :( Fond memories of other series
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1122115-allison?shelf=genre-high-fantasy">genre-high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21146505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17542652210827122977">When I picked this up, I expected to really enjoy it. After all, I like Mercedes Lackey's writing, and it had been a long time since I had read any good dragon-focused fiction. Sadly, it seems as if Lackey lifted this story from one of my favorite series of all time- The Pit Dragon Trilogy by Jane Yolen. <br/><br/>Although I will admit that the whole dragon and his boy theme is old as dirt, reading Joust was more like deja-vu than I ever could have imagined. Both stories take place in dry, arid locations </span>
  <span id="freeText17542652210827122977" style="display:none">When I picked this up, I expected to really enjoy it. After all, I like Mercedes Lackey's writing, and it had been a long time since I had read any good dragon-focused fiction. Sadly, it seems as if Lackey lifted this story from one of my favorite series of all time- The Pit Dragon Trilogy by Jane Yolen. <br /><br />Although I will admit that the whole dragon and his boy theme is old as dirt, reading Joust was more like deja-vu than I ever could have imagined. Both stories take place in dry, arid locations and focus on a serf/slave boy who finds work with dragons and eventually befriends one and raises it and trains it to fight. This story is so similar to Dragon's Blood (which I read more than ten years ago), that I honestly had to keep reminding myself they were different books. I will say that after the first book both stories go off in different directions, but at the beginning they're almost like carbon-copies of each other. It's true that Lackey's book is more political, is meant for an adult audience and is set in a very Egyptian land, but for me, that really wasn't enough of a difference. <br /><br />If I hadn't read Heart's Blood years ago, I may have rated this book higher than I did, because it's not a bad book, it's just unoriginal. But I really enjoy when authors put a twist on an old story and make it their own, and I really didn't see that happen in Joust. Fact of the matter is, I've heard this story before, and Yolen told it much better. With that in mind, I really can't rate it more than a two, because...well, it comparison, "it was (just) okay". <br /><br />Although none of the books in the series were AWFUL enough to recieve 0 or 1 star, I would say that this is the best one of the series. Unfortunately, as is typical of Lackey, the further she gets into this series, the less interested I become. I've read the first four, but after reading the last one I don't think I have any intention of reading any more about the dragon jousters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17542652210827122977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8002944471439059470">Joust drowns in its own self-righteousness.<br/><br/>Vetch is honest, kind and humble, everyone else is lazy, incompetent and ignorant. But Vetch makes these snap decisions at first sight. He decides the other dragon boys don't like him so never attempts to say hello to him, yet it's their fault that they are not friends. <br/><br/>Vetch assumes (again at first sight) that one of the overseers is concerned only with proving his status above others and will punish Vetch for any mistakes. The overseer never actually </span>
  <span id="freeText8002944471439059470" style="display:none">Joust drowns in its own self-righteousness.<br /><br />Vetch is honest, kind and humble, everyone else is lazy, incompetent and ignorant. But Vetch makes these snap decisions at first sight. He decides the other dragon boys don't like him so never attempts to say hello to him, yet it's their fault that they are not friends. <br /><br />Vetch assumes (again at first sight) that one of the overseers is concerned only with proving his status above others and will punish Vetch for any mistakes. The overseer never actually does, he leaves Vetch alone when he sees that he knows what he should be doing. <br /><br />Joust continues on like this, in fact, the vast majority of the book spends it's time hammering home how wonderful Vetch is, and how rubbish everyone around him is. It's pages and pages at a time, and it overwhelms the story.<br /><br />Somewhere in all this, there are dragons! The first 60% does it's best to ignore them, after that there is a bit more dragon time but just not enough to keep me happy. <br /><br />I shan't be continuing this series. </span>

<div id="review_179529594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179529594" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5149065-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403707173p2/5149065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179529594?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/5149065-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of The Pit Dragon Chronicles by Jane Yolen</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5149065-sarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5149065-sarah?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5149065-sarah?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179529594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17442672746933523768">Vetch, a serf working for a terrible and abusive master, knows nothing but servitude until Jouster Ari comes along. Taking Vetch under his wing, he gives him no more work than he can handle, teaches him the ways of dragons, and trusts him with the care of his dragon, Kashet. Soon after, Vetch has dreams of raising a dragon of his own.<br/><br/>I must address an issue here before I start my review. Many people see this series as comparable to <i>The Pit Dragon Chronicles</i> by Jane Yolen, and in many ways it is…</span>
  <span id="freeText17442672746933523768" style="display:none">Vetch, a serf working for a terrible and abusive master, knows nothing but servitude until Jouster Ari comes along. Taking Vetch under his wing, he gives him no more work than he can handle, teaches him the ways of dragons, and trusts him with the care of his dragon, Kashet. Soon after, Vetch has dreams of raising a dragon of his own.<br /><br />I must address an issue here before I start my review. Many people see this series as comparable to <i>The Pit Dragon Chronicles</i> by Jane Yolen, and in many ways it is… But how many vampire and werewolf books do you see these days with familiar stories and plots? This book was far original enough for me to feel like I was reading something separate and different. It evolved into it’s own type of beast. To be honest, the hope that this series would be similar to <i>The Pit Dragon Chronicles</i> is what originally attracted me to it. I was very delighted to give it a try! <i>Joust</i> did not disappoint!<br /><br />Normally I would remove a star for this book not having some sort of love story, but it doesn’t need it!! Vetch’s developing passion for dragons took that place for me. I don’t know how Lackey did it, but I was hooked... This book became like a drug for me. I couldn’t stop reading! And yes, because of the attachment to the characters, I did cry.. but only once.<br /><br />The one problem I have is with the cover. The dragon looks great, but the man on the front is nothing like how I pictured a jouster. Ok, maybe it’s just the helmet... I don’t think I’d want to look like I was wearing a freakin’ vase on my head. Real intimidating. Just my personal opinion.<br /><br />I’ve read Mercedes Lackey’s books in the past and liked them, but where was this series all my life!? The characters, setting, and plot were all perfectly conceived to build this sure-to-be epic series. I love how <i>Joust</i> ended and cannot wait to delve back into this amazing world. <br /><br />See my other reviews at <a href="http://inklingsread.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Inklings Read.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17442672746933523768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_570934538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570934538" />
    <a title="Kelsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5729301-kelsey"><img alt="Kelsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404168912p2/5729301.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570934538?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey" href="/user/show/5729301-kelsey">Kelsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570934538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11080272551134583785">I haven’t read that many Mercedes Lackey books, even though she’s one of the most popular and prolific fantasy writers today. I picked up <i>Joust</i> for $1 during a Borders closing sale. The plot follows Vetch, a young serf plucked from his cruel master’s yard to become a dragon boy to the jouster Ari and dragon Kashet. The world is Ancient Egypt with a little magic and a few flying serpents.<br/><br/>The beginning is slow. Very slow. It takes 23 pages for Vetch to fetch a bucket of water. Of course, if someon</span>
  <span id="freeText11080272551134583785" style="display:none">I haven’t read that many Mercedes Lackey books, even though she’s one of the most popular and prolific fantasy writers today. I picked up <i>Joust</i> for $1 during a Borders closing sale. The plot follows Vetch, a young serf plucked from his cruel master’s yard to become a dragon boy to the jouster Ari and dragon Kashet. The world is Ancient Egypt with a little magic and a few flying serpents.<br /><br />The beginning is slow. Very slow. It takes 23 pages for Vetch to fetch a bucket of water. Of course, if someone had to describe fetching water for 23 pages, Mercedes Lackey is a good choice, but even so I was getting antsy.<br /><br />Chapter 9 is the turning point. Until then, the book creeps along, still interesting in its way, like floating a canoe down a lazy river. Then in Chapter 9 (literally almost exactly halfway through: page 210 for a 442-page book), the story picks up, and you’re paddling frantically through rapids. They’re not Class VI by any means, but the contrast between the first half of the book and the second was so disjointed that it made the first half seem worse by comparison. Vetch spends so much time trying to be good and responsible, laying low, and figuring things out, and then in the second half all his well-laid plans yield bountiful crops one right after the other.<br /><br />I liked exploring the Egyptian fantasy land, a fascinating change from typical European Medieval world, and I enjoyed the unique day-to-day of jouster society. Still, the stakes were never high enough, I liked but didn’t love the characters, and the pace was too uneven. An interesting read but not a favorite.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11080272551134583785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_1380727017" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1380727017" />
    <a title="Khari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16880570-khari"><img alt="Khari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473471301p2/16880570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380727017?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khari" href="/user/show/16880570-khari">Khari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16880570-khari?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380727017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7149980723135314392">That was great.<br/><br/>I've been reading so much manga lately that I apparently got fed up. I needed something in English! A novel, something where I made up everything in my head, not just the bits in the gutter between the panels.<br/><br/>I haven't read this series in a while. I've always adored Lackey since the first time I picked up her books on Valdemar, but the Jouster series holds a special place in my heart. I mean it's set in an alternate Egypt...with dragons! How could it possibly get better?! You have</span>
  <span id="freeText7149980723135314392" style="display:none">That was great.<br /><br />I've been reading so much manga lately that I apparently got fed up. I needed something in English! A novel, something where I made up everything in my head, not just the bits in the gutter between the panels.<br /><br />I haven't read this series in a while. I've always adored Lackey since the first time I picked up her books on Valdemar, but the Jouster series holds a special place in my heart. I mean it's set in an alternate Egypt...with dragons! How could it possibly get better?! You have the ephemeral allure of Egyptian deserts, gods and customs, and dragons! Absolute win!<br /><br />The other thing is that Lackey is very good at creating a world that you can believe in. Her characters have real moral struggles and you never quite know whether they will come out on top of them or not.<br /><br />I believe this is actually my third time through this series, but this was the first time that I read it with any sort of psychological lens. I found some interesting things. I found this quote "Words had power, and names were the most powerful of all words. Words were what the gods used to shape the world." I thought this was really interesting. Lackey does not seem to be of any particular religious bent, yet I find it interesting that in this book her world is created by logos, the spoken word. It's interesting how this is a truth that people keep coming back to, it's an idea that pops up again and again, in the Bible, in the Dresden books, in movies like Arrival, in books like Lawhead's work. It's just interesting that it keeps popping up. Is this idea also an archetype? Maybe.<br /><br />Another one that I quite liked was the moral struggle that Ari faces when he hears about the Jousters committing atrocious acts of genocide, he runs away, he abandons his responsibilities and screams in his agony, and then he has to come to a decision about what he will do. He cannot rely on anyone else, he cannot be guided in the right way, he must himself choose to do what is right. I thought that was a powerful scene.<br /><br />The last powerful scene for me was when Vetch is screaming out his rage about his people being murdered. He is writhing in pain and rises from his crushed state motivated by resentment and anger, determined to take revenge on those that have hurt his tribe, and then he pauses. He weighs the import of his decisions, he realizes that he cannot take revenge, because then he would be the same as those he hates. He realizes that he cannot put his fantasies into practice because to do so would be to corrupt his own soul. It was a great scene. <br /><br />I love it when fantasy authors do things like this with their work. The lessons in this book are the same lessons that were taught by Sozhenitsyn in his work, the line of good and evil runs down the heart of each human. The lesson is no less real than because it is embedded in a fantastical world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7149980723135314392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_305615584" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305615584" />
    <a title="Dani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7794425-dani"><img alt="Dani" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305615584?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani" href="/user/show/7794425-dani">Dani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305615584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12143630919623079967">Have you ever gotten that feeling, after finishing a book? That amazing feeling, of "wow." Simple amazement, and knowledge that what you have just read will remain with you forever? That's how I felt after gently closing the cover of <i> Joust </i> by Mercedes Lackey. Interestingly, if you ask me for a list of my all-time favorite books, fully half would be written by Lackey, while the other half is pulled from every author, genre, and intended audience. This book was certainly one of my very favorite.</span>
  <span id="freeText12143630919623079967" style="display:none">Have you ever gotten that feeling, after finishing a book? That amazing feeling, of "wow." Simple amazement, and knowledge that what you have just read will remain with you forever? That's how I felt after gently closing the cover of <i> Joust </i> by Mercedes Lackey. Interestingly, if you ask me for a list of my all-time favorite books, fully half would be written by Lackey, while the other half is pulled from every author, genre, and intended audience. This book was certainly one of my very favorite. It depicts Vetch, a serf in the land of Tia (serf being a lower class then slave.) He dreams of times past when he lived with his family on a farm in Alta. But Tia and Alta are at war, and Alta is slowly but surely falling under the stronger hand of the Tians. Perhaps the war wouldn't be going so badly for the Altans, if not for the Jousters. Long ago, before anyone can remember, someone discovered the secret to taming and riding dragons--and it all lives in a simple plant with a bitter drug--tala. Tala, when ground to a powder and added to the dragons food, has a remarkable effect on the dragons--drugging them into accepting riders, who in turn fly them to war. the Tian Jousters greatly outnumber their Altan counterparts, and that is why Vetch is a serf. One day, when Vetch is slaving under his cruel master, a Jouster lands before his eyes--Ari--and takes him away to be a dragon boy to Ari and his dragon Kashet. Vetch is supposed to care for both dragon and Jouster, and see that they are always fit and ready for battle. But Vetch is Altan, and Ari is Tian. A war arises inside Vetch himself, and he knows not how to fight it. All he knows is that a strange sort of friendship is growing between him and Ari, and as for Kashet, Well, Kashet is not like other dragons. Not at all. Instead of being caught wild and drugged into submission, Kashet was hatched by Ari, and raised by him from the egg, making him the only truly tame dragon in the world. Vetch likes Kashet, and the feeling is mutual. At nights, Ari comes to Kashet's pen and talks to him and Vetch about one thing--dragons. For Ari has a passion for the animals, and soon, so does Vetch. Soon, Vetch hatches a plan to hatch his own tame dragon, and escape with her to Alta when she fledges. The rest of the book is wrapped up in how Vetch pull off this plan, hatching the amazing scarlet dragon he names Avatre, and how he attempts to escape on her back, with all the Jousters following in his wake, trying to stop him. He manages to outdistance all but one--Ari. The dramatic close to the book is exactly what is needed in such a place, and it left me with an immense feeling of satisfaction, and the knowledge that this book would not remain on my shelf for long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12143630919623079967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="K H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17950886-k-h"><img alt="K H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427124891p2/17950886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010392347?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K H" href="/user/show/17950886-k-h">K H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010392347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12501780500644714545">I liked Joust.<br/><br/>This was my first read of Lackey's and I enjoined it well enough. The few characters (3-4) that were developed were three dimensional and real enough. The plot was good, <i>if not fast paced</i>, and the world building/dragon knowledge well thought through.<br/><br/>What took this down from a five star?<br/><br/>I could probably summarize this 373 page book in less than five plot points. It was definitely slow moving, and I can't help but feel it would have been better if it was a little hacked down and its </span>
  <span id="freeText12501780500644714545" style="display:none">I liked Joust.<br /><br />This was my first read of Lackey's and I enjoined it well enough. The few characters (3-4) that were developed were three dimensional and real enough. The plot was good, <i>if not fast paced</i>, and the world building/dragon knowledge well thought through.<br /><br />What took this down from a five star?<br /><br />I could probably summarize this 373 page book in less than five plot points. It was definitely slow moving, and I can't help but feel it would have been better if it was a little hacked down and its sequel was tacked onto the end. That being said, Lackey's writing never left me bored, just a bit disappointed in its slower pace.<br /><br />What really levelled Joust down from a love to a like for me was the <b>repetition</b>. I kid you not, every thought, memory, or feeling of Vetch's is rethought of <i>
  <b>at least twice</b>
</i> in the novel, which is fairly annoying if you're reading it in a shorter time period. In this way though, if you're reading more than one book, Joust is the perfect one to have on the back burner without fear of forgetting important tidbits.<br /><br />Overall, this probably won't be a series I'm going to reread, but Lackey's writing makes it worth continuing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12501780500644714545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Schwabauer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Schwabauer" href="/user/show/14650879-daniel-schwabauer">Daniel Schwabauer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699560823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8341019127592514512">The care and feeding of dragons in ancient Egypt.<br/><br/>This book was my first experience with the work of Mercedes Lackey. Joust is moderately enjoyable, in spite of the fact that very little actually happens in it. Presumably this is because the author is using the story to set up a larger series, but I would have preferred half as many words and twice as much conflict.<br/><br/>That said, it is probably to the author's credit that she was able to drag me through 400+ pages of internal monologues. (The first 2</span>
  <span id="freeText8341019127592514512" style="display:none">The care and feeding of dragons in ancient Egypt.<br /><br />This book was my first experience with the work of Mercedes Lackey. Joust is moderately enjoyable, in spite of the fact that very little actually happens in it. Presumably this is because the author is using the story to set up a larger series, but I would have preferred half as many words and twice as much conflict.<br /><br />That said, it is probably to the author's credit that she was able to drag me through 400+ pages of internal monologues. (The first 23 pages chronicle nothing except the main character fetching a pail of water. But I kept reading.)<br /><br />I did enjoy her handling of forgiveness and the danger of misidentifying one's enemies. I also thought her treatment of dragon taming was fun, though not particularly unique. For that matter, most of the plot twists were predictable, though handled skillfully. Her worldbuilding is engrossing (though at one point she uses accusations of witchcraft to imply that certain people are narrow-minded and superstitious; later we learn that actual witches are causing all the big storms.) <br /><br />No regrets about time spent on this one, but I doubt I will continue with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8341019127592514512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17726027736106544335" style="display:none">For the first time ever, national best-selling legend Mercedes Lackey draws from her extensive knowlege of animals and her professional background as an<br />avian expert-to create something truly special…<br /><br />The most exciting, authentic and believable portrayal of dragons ever imagined.<br /><br />It is a richly conceived, fully realized vision, inspired by the culture of ancient Egypt, the legends of Atlantis--and the science of animal behavior and<br />biology. This is how dragons would live, breed, hatch, hunt, and bond.<br /><br />The first book in this thrilling new series introduces readers to a young slave who dreams of becoming a Jouster--one of the few warriors who can actually<br />ride a flying dragon. And so, in secret, he begins to raise his own dragon.<br />I originally read a short story based on this book by Mercedes Lackey in an anthology of dragon stories. I thought the way the story ended was the way the book would end but I was glad it did not. I was even more thrilled to know this is a series and I have gathered the rest of the books to read.</span>

  <span id="freeText2374325207513666134" style="display:none">Wonderful book! <br /><br />My heart was breaking for Vetch several times and I was so happy when Ari saved him and took him to the compound to become a dragon-boy - which led to more heartbreak. *g*<br /><br />I like Vetch and Ari - the two main characters. <div id="review_139307293" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139307293" />
    <a title="♆ BookAddict  ✒ La Crimson Femme" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3089655-bookaddict-la-crimson-femme"><img alt="♆ BookAddict  ✒ La Crimson Femme" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537761015p2/3089655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139307293?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♆ BookAddict  ✒ La Crimson Femme" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♆ BookAddict  ✒ La Crimson Femme" href="/user/show/3089655-bookaddict-la-crimson-femme">♆ BookAddict  ✒ La Crimson Femme</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3089655-bookaddict-la-crimson-femme?shelf=dragon">dragon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3089655-bookaddict-la-crimson-femme?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139307293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10754676860018138585">New series by Ms. Lackey is awesome! I'm rating this a 3.5 but since I only round down, it's showing up as a three. I loved the attention to detail on showing how to take care of a dragon. The opposing forces are ominous. I know which side I'd pick. This book reminded me of Ms. McCaffrey's dragon singer series. When Menolly raised the fire dragons, this book is similar in several ways. Enjoyed it and can't wait for the next one.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R0g/pJcV45quWDR5TUdz+v6DP/f1dHh02tDjQAKONlzRi03IQMEtNqxyJbOkjPGlw4RNeu5BuO6wXMD4/NcPlw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Nhkv4FTRwtFoa12cjRL82yWWQLNK4ipporA5boK8oNeg2l2MgwUMfWpBTFZk2X6EGJEyPlHX6vPIPBrWfOWZHA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey">About Mercedes Lackey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1215643156p3/8685.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8109083714826315319">Mercedes entered this world on June 24, 1950, in Chicago, had a normal childhood and graduated from Purdue University in 1972. During the late 70's she worked as an artist's model and then went into the computer programming field, ending up with American Airlines in Tulsa, Oklahoma. In addition to her fantasy writing, she has written lyrics for and recorded nearly fifty songs for Firebird Arts & M</span>
  <span id="freeText8109083714826315319" style="display:none">Mercedes entered this world on June 24, 1950, in Chicago, had a normal childhood and graduated from Purdue University in 1972. During the late 70's she worked as an artist's model and then went into the computer programming field, ending up with American Airlines in Tulsa, Oklahoma. In addition to her fantasy writing, she has written lyrics for and recorded nearly fifty songs for Firebird Arts &amp; Music, a small recording company specializing in science fiction folk music.<br /><br />"I'm a storyteller; that's what I see as 'my job'. My stories come out of my characters; how those characters would react to the given situation. Maybe that's why I get letters from readers as young as thirteen and as old as sixty-odd. One of the reasons I write song lyrics is because I see songs as a kind of 'story pill' -- they reduce a story to the barest essentials or encapsulate a particular crucial moment in time. I frequently will write a lyric when I am attempting to get to the heart of a crucial scene; I find that when I have done so, the scene has become absolutely clear in my mind, and I can write exactly what I wanted to say. Another reason is because of the kind of novels I am writing: that is, fantasy, set in an other-world semi-medieval atmosphere. Music is very important to medieval peoples; bards are the chief newsbringers. When I write the 'folk music' of these peoples, I am enriching my whole world, whether I actually use the song in the text or not.<br /><br />"I began writing out of boredom; I continue out of addiction. I can't 'not' write, and as a result I have no social life! I began writing fantasy because I love it, but I try to construct my fantasy worlds with all the care of a 'high-tech' science fiction writer. I apply the principle of TANSTAAFL ['There ain't no such thing as free lunch', credited to Robert Heinlein) to magic, for instance; in my worlds, magic is paid for, and the cost to the magician is frequently a high one. I try to keep my world as solid and real as possible; people deal with stubborn pumps, bugs in the porridge, and love-lives that refuse to become untangled, right along with invading armies and evil magicians. And I try to make all of my characters, even the 'evil magicians,' something more than flat stereotypes. Even evil magicians get up in the night and look for cookies, sometimes.<br /><br />"I suppose that in everything I write I try to expound the creed I gave my character Diana Tregarde in <i>Burning Water</i>:<br /><br />"There's no such thing as 'one, true way'; the only answers worth having are the ones you find for yourself; leave the world better than you found it. Love, freedom, and the chance to do some good -- they're the things worth living and dying for, and if you aren't willing to die for the things worth living for, you might as well turn in your membership in the human race." <br /><br />Also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2504886.Misty_Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Misty Lackey</a><br /><br /><a href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/mercedeslackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Author's website</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8109083714826315319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13996.Alta"><img alt="Alta (Dragon Jousters, #2)" style="height: 75px;" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1388335863l/13996._SY75_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_13996'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13996.Alta?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Alta (Dragon Jousters, #2)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey?origin=series_works\">Mercedes Lackey<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.04 avg rating &mdash; 7,697 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2004\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer8078446141202832331\">DRAGON RIDER\n\nVetch had done the unimaginable. He had secretly raised his own baby dragon, a crimson female he named Avatre, and when she first took flight he had been on her back. Although Avatre was new to flight, with the help of his trainer and f<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8078446141202832331\" style=\"display:none\">DRAGON RIDER\n\nVetch had done the unimaginable. He had secretly raised his own baby dragon, a crimson female he named Avatre, and when she first took flight he had been on her back. Although Avatre was new to flight, with the help of his trainer and friend, the dragon Jouster Ari, he had managed to evade pursuit, escaping from the compound that housed the dragon-riding troops of Tia, his homeland\'s enemies. Aided by the nomadic tribes of the desert, Vetch and Avatre had crossed the vast sands heading north toward the lands still held by Alta.\n\nIt was Vetch\'s plan to convey to his half-conquered homeland the secret which he hoped would be the key to Alta\'s liberation: how to tame dragons. If he imparted this secret to the Altan rulers, would it not give them the edge they needed to throw off their conquerors despite their lesser numbers? And it seemed that his good luck was holding when, after saving a young priestess of noble blood from the dangers of the Great Mother River, he was given entree into the dragon Jouster compound of Alta City.\n\nBut Vetch, now calling himself by his birth name of Kiron was completely ignorant of the true forces that controlled Alta. For though the royal Great Ones sat on the Altan throne, they did not truly rule. In Alta the Magi, the all- powerful practitioners of sorcery, held the populace--royalty and commoner alike--under the sway of a mysterious weapon.
